1001 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Hudson Properties Co. v. Governing Bd.


Civ. No. 51648


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


168 Cal. App. 3d 63; 213 Cal. Rptr. 909; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2071



May 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of plaintiff and appellant for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 434178, Read Ambler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's decision that District's agreement to sell the property to Maroviches was void, 15 and direct the trial court to order District to hold a session for final acceptance pursuant to section 39375, as discussed herein. In addition, the parties may petition the trial court for leave to file supplemental pleadings on the question of an equitable accounting. Upon such further proceedings as the trial court may deem appropriate, it may act on that issue.



15 The trial court, as noted earlier, found section 39369.5 to be unconstitutional and determined that it had no authority to compel a sale by District. We, of course, did not address these issues, but "'a ruling or decision, itself correct in law, will not be disturbed on appeal merely because given for a wrong reason. If right upon any theory of the law applicable to the case, it must be sustained regardless of the considerations which may have moved the trial court to its conclusion.'" ( D'Amico v. Board of Medical Examiners (1974) 11 Cal.3d 1, 19 [112 Cal.Rptr. 786, 520 P.2d 10].)

 [***2]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which declared Cal. Educ. Code § 39369.5 unconstitutional and negated the rights of the original sellers to purchase property from defendant school district. Plaintiff corporation filed a cross-appeal from the portion of the judgment holding that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to order defendant school district to sell the property to it.


OVERVIEW: Defendant school district purchased property from previous owners, and thereafter found that it did not need the property. The previous owners entered into an option contract, whereby they would repurchase the property under their rights pursuant to Cal. Educ. Code § 39369.5, and then resell the property to defendant corporation. Plaintiff corporation submitted the high bid and the previous owners attempted to exercise their repurchase rights. Plaintiff then filed an action before the trial court seeking an injunction, and judgment in its favor, contending that the previous owners' option was actually an assignment of rights and was unenforceable as in conflict with § 39369.5. On appeal, the court held that the statute conferred a personal right on the previous owner and that an assignment would not be valid. The court held that because the option contract gave all of the previous owners' rights to defendant corporation, and defendant corporation was to provide the purchase money and pay all transfer and escrow costs, the option was an assignment, and therefore was not enforceable against defendant district. The court affirmed the decision voiding resale to the previous owners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that defendant school district's agreement to resell property to the previous sellers was void, and directed trial court to order defendant district to hold a session for final acceptance. Defendant district could accept or reject plaintiff corporation's bid. While the statute was retroactive to previous sellers, their rights were personal and non-assignable, and their option to defendant corporation was invalid.

 

1002 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Dep't of Health Servs. v. Fontes


No. A028019


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


169 Cal. App. 3d 301; 215 Cal. Rptr. 14; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1997



May 13, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 505961, Peter G. Stone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate executor sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), holding that Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 14009.5, 1981 Cal. Stat. 102, § 101 (amended by 1981 Cal. Stat. 1163, § 3) gave respondent Department of Health Services a claim to reimbursement for Medi-Cal benefits from an estate when the recipient died after the effective date of § 14009.5 but benefits were received before the effective date.


OVERVIEW: A woman received Medi-Cal benefits while she was alive. When she died, appellant estate executor rejected respondent Department of Health Services' claim for reimbursement against the estate. The claim was made under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 14009.5, 1981 Cal. Stat. 102, § 101 (amended by 1981 Cal. Stat. 1163, § 3). Appellant maintained that only Medi-Cal benefits received after the effective date of the statute were subject to a claim for reimbursement. The trial court ruled that respondent had a right to reimbursement. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed. The court held that the interpretation of a statute by the officials charged with its application has to be given great weight. The court found that the legislature did not intend to make § 14009.5 retroactive. But the court found that § 14009.5 did not have any impermissible retroactive effect. Any right that the woman recipient had in the disposition of her estate was defined partially by the version of § 14009.5 in effect at the time of her death. Furthermore, § 14009.5 did not retroactively affect any existing rights held by the woman's estate because the estate did not come into existence until her death.


OUTCOME: Ruling against appellant estate executor and in favor of respondent Department of Health Services, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the application of the statute in question to estates that arose after its effective date did not affect any existing rights to benefits, and, therefore, the statute was prospective as intended and did not have any impermissible retroactive effect.

 

1003 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Building Industry Ass'n v. City of Camarillo


No. B004233.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


168 Cal. App. 3d 27; 213 Cal. Rptr. 816; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2068



May 10, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rev. granted Aug. 22, 1985 (See 41 Cal. 3d 810)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, Nos. 74162 and 77065, William L. Peck, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a building industry association, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), granting partial summary judgment in favor of respondent, the city of Camarillo, finding that Cal. Evid. Code § 669.5 and Cal. Gov't Code § 65863.6 did not apply to initiative ordinances, specifically Measure A, a growth ordinance enacted by the voters of respondent.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, the City of Camarillo, enacted a growth ordinance known as Measure A, limiting the number of buildable lots. Measure A was enacted by the voters pursuant to their initiative power. Appellant, a building industry association, challenged the validity of Measure A. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that Cal. Evid. Code § 669.5 and Cal. Gov't Code § 65863.6 did not apply to initiative actions. The court adopted the construction of § 669.5 and § 65863.6 that eliminated doubts as to the provisions' constitutionality. The court found that Measure A was an initiative ordinance and was not enacted by the "governing body" of respondent, as required in § 669.5. The court also found that under § 65863.6, what was in the minds of the electorate in adopting the initiative was immaterial. No one contended that the enactment of Measure A did not comply with the state initiative law, and if the legislature wanted zoning regulations adopted by initiative to go through the process specified in § 65863.6, the initiative law was the place to specify this requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment in favor of respondent, the city of Camarillo. Statutory provision that would have placed the burden of proof on respondent to show that a growth ordinance was necessary for the protection of the public health, safety, or welfare, was not applicable to an initiative ordinance, because it was approved by the voters and not enacted by the "governing body" of respondent.

 

1004 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Figueroa


Crim. No. F003167.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH Dist.


167 Cal. App. 3d 981; 213 Cal. Rptr. 676; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2039



May 3, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Parts III and IV are not published, as they do not meet the standard of publication contained in rule 976(b), California Rules of Court.


Rev. den. Aug. 1, 1985 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 24475, James G. Bowles, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which convicted her willful cruelty or unjustifiable punishment of child, endangering life or health of a child in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 273a(1) and imposed a prison sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and her boyfriend were charged with crimes stemming from her boyfriend's abuse of her son. The court affirmed appellant's conviction because the conduct required for a violation of Cal. Penal Code §273a(1) was not that of intent, but rather of negligent omission to do something the surrounding circumstances would demand of a reasonable person. In this case, appellant allowed the abuse to happen. The court held that the defendant was on notice that she was charged with willfully permitting her child to be injured, as well as willfully allowing him to be endangered and she could be convicted on proof of willfully permitting specific incidents to occur or, in the alternative, of permitting the child's person and health to be endangered. The court held the charge involved required no proof of aiding or encouragement of the party directly inflicting the abuse. The court determined there were no instructional errors requiring reversal; however, it noted that juror confusion could be avoided if the two theories of criminal responsibility were better contrasted by separating the instructions into one series on purposeful conduct and one series on culpable negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for willful cruelty or unjustifiable punishment of child, endangering life or health of a child, because she allowed the abuse to take place and the charge required no proof of her aiding or encouraging her boyfriend in inflicting the abuse.

 

1005 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Corbett v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. B005216.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


167 Cal. App. 3d 808; 213 Cal. Rptr. 893; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2027



May 2, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. den. Aug. 22, 1985 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 289871, Norman R. Dowds, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant California State Franchise Board challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles (California), which concluded appellee taxpayers were not liable for personal income tax assessments made by appellant and that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1060.5 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers filed an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant California State Franchise Board alleging that defendant's personal income tax assessments against them were erroneous because they were not residents of California. The trial court granted judgment in favor of plaintiffs. Upon appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Cal. Civ. Proc. § 1060.50, which provided for declaratory and injunctive relief to challenge income tax assessments on the grounds of residency was constitutional. The court reasoned that under the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV nonresidents were entitled to substantive due process and that the anti-injunction provision of Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 32 yielded to the paramount provisions of the United States Constitution. The court found plaintiffs were residents of Illinois because they had the closest connection to that state where they maintained a house in Illinois, and had substantial business and personal interests there. The court held plaintiffs did not engage in conduct that made them more than seasonal visitors to California.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that concluded plaintiff taxpayers were not liable for personal income tax assessments made by defendant California State Franchise Board. The court held a statute that provided injunctive and declaratory relief was constitutional where it afforded substantive due process protection to nonresidents. The court found that plaintiffs were nonresidents of California because they had closer connections to Illinois.

 

1006 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Hesslink


Crim. No. 16226


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


167 Cal. App. 3d 781; 213 Cal. Rptr. 465; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2025



May 1, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 17, 1985, and the petitions of all parties for review by the Supreme Court were denied August 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR 20464, John H. Barnard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction of extortion ( Pen. Code, § 518) is reversed and the sentence imposed thereon is vacated. Defendant must be resentenced only if he is again tried and convicted of the extortion charge. If he is not retried or not again convicted of the extortion charge, the abstract of judgment must be amended to eliminate the extortion conviction and the sentence imposed thereon. In all other respects the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) that convicted him of forcible oral copulation, extortion, and impersonating a police officer. Sentence was imposed accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Defendant picked up a prostitute, displayed a badge to her, and made her orally copulate him. A jury found defendant guilty of forcible oral copulation, impersonating a police officer, and extortion. The reviewing court reversed defendant's conviction of extortion and vacated the sentence, but otherwise affirmed. Defendant should not have been convicted of extortion because the trial court had not instructed the jury as to specific intent, an element of extortion. This error was prejudicial, especially because the victim testified that she gave defendant money without his asking for it. The evidence that the victim's mouth touched defendant's penis was sufficient to support his conviction for forcible oral copulation. Although the trial court should have deleted the reference to force, violence, and fear of immediate bodily harm from the jury instruction on forcible oral copulation because they were inconsistent with the prosecution's theories, the error was harmless and the jury could not have been misled. The trial court could not avoid denying probation under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.065(a), and that statute's prohibition of probation was not cruel or unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of extortion because the failure to instruct the jury on specific intent was reversible error, and it therefore vacated his sentence. The court affirmed otherwise, because there was sufficient evidence of forcible oral copulation and a statute required denial of probation.

 

1007 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



In re John V.


Civ. No. 31417


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


167 Cal. App. 3d 761; 213 Cal. Rptr. 503; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2023



May 1, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. J 116539, Gilbert D. Smith, Judge, Juvenile Court Referee.



DISPOSITION: The probation condition preventing John from talking or commenting about W. out of her presence is stricken. Except as modified the order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), finding that he violated Cal. Penal Code § 415(3), which prohibited the use of offensive words in a public place which were inherently likely to provoke an immediate violent reaction. Appellant contended the statute violated his rights under U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 7(a).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found appellant juvenile violated Cal. Penal Code § 415(3), which precluded the use of offensive words in a public place which were inherently likely to provoke an immediate violent reaction. Appellant had called his neighbor a "fucking bitch," which caused her to become incoherent, enraged, and humiliated. Appellant sought review, contending that the statute was unconstitutional as overbroad, in violation of his rights under U.S. Const. amend. I and Cal. Const. art. I, § 2(a), and that it was vague, in violation of U.S. Const. art. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7(a). The court affirmed the decision, finding that the statute was not overbroad and did not violate appellant's right to free speech because that right did not protect words specifically addressed to another spoken under circumstances which created a clear and present danger that violence would imminently erupt. The court determined that the statute was not vague because it gave fair notice to appellant what he could and could not lawfully say in a public place.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that found appellant juvenile violated the statute that proscribed the use of offensive words in a public place which were inherently likely to provoke an immediate violent reaction. The court found the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The court determined that appellant had fair notice that his utterance would provoke a violent reaction from the victim of his verbal abuse.

 

1008 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Westminster Mobile Home Park Owners' Ass'n v. City of Westminster


Civ. No. 30081.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


167 Cal. App. 3d 610; 213 Cal. Rptr. 640; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1967



April 30, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As modified May 14, 1985; Rev. den. July 30, 1985, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 359572, Thomas F. Crosby, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile home park appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) that granted judgment of the pleadings in favor of defendants city in an action to have defendant city's mobile home rent control program declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city enacted a rent control program for mobile home parks. Under the programs, any increase in rents had to be approved by 51 percent of the homeowners in the park. If the homeowner's did not consent, compulsory arbitration was required before an independent arbitrator who was not connected to defendant. Either party could seek judicial review of the arbitrator's decision. Plaintiff mobile home park filed suit to challenge the constitutionality of defendant's program. The trial court entered judgment in favor of defendant. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that plaintiff was not required to exhaust its administrative remedies prior to bringing a claim of facial unconstitutionality. The court held that the adjustment mechanism provided in the rent control program was unconstitutional because it could result in unreasonable delay. The court recognized that a final decision could take over a year to be reached. The court also held that the program was unconstitutional because defendant retained no control over the program to assure that the policies and standards contained in the applicable ordinances were carried out.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court against plaintiff mobile home park. The adjustment mechanism provided in defendant city's mobile home rent control program was unconstitutional because it necessarily resulted in needless and unreasonable delay and because defendant retained no control over the program to assure that it was properly carried out.

 

1009 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Mueller v. Walker


Civ. No. 31374


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


167 Cal. App. 3d 600; 213 Cal. Rptr. 442; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1966



April 30, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N 22708, Ross G. Tharp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed a decision from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which held that defendant husband's military retirement benefits were his separate property and not subject to division in a divorce proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife and defendant husband were divorced. Based on a court decision, the trial court determined that defendant's military pension was his separate property and not subject to division. Plaintiff contended that the Federal Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act (Act), 10 U.S.C. § 1408, should be applied retroactively. The Act provided that military retirement benefits could be deemed community property, subject to division. On appeal, the court reversed the decision. The divorce decree had to be modified to include a division of defendant's military retirement benefits. The divorce decree was entered during the interim period after the court decision and before the effective date of the Act. Cal. Civ. Code § 5124 specifically provided that the Act be given retroactive effect during the interim period. It was not Congress' intent to bar claims for community property interests just because the parties' divorce decrees were entered during the interim period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that defendant husband's military retirement benefits were defendant's separate property because a state statute specifically provided that the Federal Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act was to be given retroactive effect for the 18 month period before its effective date. Defendant's military retirement benefits were subject to division in the parties' divorce proceeding.

 

1010 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Harrison v. County of Del Norte


No. A018319


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


168 Cal. App. 3d 1; 213 Cal. Rptr. 658; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2065



April 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 30, 1985, and the opinion was modified to read as printed above. Poche, Acting P. J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted. Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 19, 1985. Bird, C. J., Mosk, J., and Reynoso, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Del Norte County, No. 82121, Thomas M. Montgomery, Judge. *


* Retired judge of the superior court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Del Norte County (California) which denied appellant relief from the claim presentation requirement of Cal. Gov't Code § 945.4.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was working for appellee county when he was injured. Appellant failed to file claims with appellee within 100 days of the injury, as required by Cal. Gov't Code § 945.4. The trial court denied appellant's application for leave to file a late claim brought pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 945.6. Appellant claimed that his failure to timely file a claim was due to mistake or excusable neglect. Appellant did not know the limitations period for filing a claim and did not seek counsels' advice until after the 100 day period had expired. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Appellant's mere ignorance of the time limitation for filing did not constitute mistake or excusable neglect. To obtain relief under § 945.6, appellant had to make some effort to obtain legal counsel within the 100 days. Appellant also could have discovered the time limitation with a little diligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision because appellant employee's failure to file his claim against appellee county within the 100-day time limitation was due to inexcusable neglect. Appellant's ignorance of the time limitation for filing and his failure to timely seek counsel did not constitute mistake or excusable neglect.

 

1011 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



City of Vallejo v. Adult Books


No. A021042


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


167 Cal. App. 3d 1169; 213 Cal. Rptr. 143; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2058



April 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 22, 1985. Racanelli, P. J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted. Appellants' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 17, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Solano County, No. VO2157, Michael L. McInnis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult book stores sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Solano County (California), which upheld the constitutionality of an ordinance enacted by respondent city council after appellant challenged its constitutionality on grounds that it was vague and violative of U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Appellant adult book stores challenged the constitutionality of an ordinance enacted by respondent city council on grounds that it was vague and violative of U.S. Const. amend. I. The court concluded that the challenged language did not so threaten U.S. Const. amend. I rights as to permit a challenge to its clarity by an enterprise such as appellant, which uncontestably fell within its regulatory scope. Accordingly, the court found that appellant lacked standing to challenge the ordinance on vagueness grounds. The court held that the ordinance was a content-neutral regulation of the time, place, and manner of protected speech and not a direct abrogation or infringement of U.S. Const. amend. I rights. Permissible locations available to adult users were restricted by the ordinance, but not legislated out of existence. The court was also convinced that the ordinance would not result in an oppressive and unconstitutional restriction of public access to adult material. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellant adult book stores challenging the constitutionality of an ordinance enacted by respondent city council on grounds that it was vague and violative of the First Amendment. The court held that appellant lacked standing to challenge the ordinance on vagueness grounds and that the ordinance was a content-neutral regulation of the time, place, and manner of protected speech.

 

1012 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Roehler


Crim. No. 43117


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


167 Cal. App. 3d 353; 213 Cal. Rptr. 353; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1946



April 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied May 22, 1985, and the opinion was modified to read as printed above. Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 19, 1985. Bird, C. J., Mosk, J., and Kaus, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Barbara County, No. 136863, John T. Rickard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for the first degree murders of his wife and son obtained in the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California) and alleged, among other things, that the county coroner's office had violated U.S. Const. amend IV. and Cal. Const. art. I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder for the deaths of his wife and son. Defendant argued, among other things, that the seizure and autopsies of the bodies of his wife and son by the county coroner-sheriff violated the rights guaranteed him by U.S. Const. amend. IV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 13. The court held that the coroner, like other governmental officials, was subject to U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court held, however, that the coroner's conduct was proper because he had a made a proper application for and a proper warrant was issued, which allowed the seizure and search of the victims' bodies. Defendant's other points of error were overruled by the court, and accordingly the judgment of conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed because no reversible error was found. Defendant's Fourth Amendment rights had not been violated because proper warrants had been issued that allowed the county coroner to conduct autopsies on defendant's wife and son.

 

1013 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



In re Bank of San Marino


Civ. No. B003211


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


167 Cal. App. 3d 247; 213 Cal. Rptr. 602; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1938



April 24, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C448913, Leon Savitch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which approved the sale of certain assets and the transfer of certain liabilities of appellant to another bank, after respondent Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation filed a petition seeking to have the sale approved.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation filed a petition seeking to have the trial court approve a sale of certain assets and a transfer of certain liabilities of appellant bank to another bank. Respondent gave notice to appellant's president and counsel of the hearing, but was told that they would not attend the hearing. The trial court approved the sale and transfer. Appellant argued that respondent's petition was insufficient as a matter of law to support the order and that it was denied due process because the lower court failed to stay its order under Cal. Fin. Code § 3101. The court affirmed, finding that the petition was sufficient to support the order and that appellant failed to demonstrate any omission, flaw, or viable alternative available to respondent. The court found that appellant was given adequate notice of the hearing and that appellant chose not to appear or request a continuance. Section 3101 did not provide an automatic stay, but rather a statute of limitations in which appellant may file an action. Cal. Fin. Cod § 3110.1 authorized the immediate consummation of a purchase and assumption agreement notwithstanding the provisions of § 3101.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order approving the sale of assets and transfer of liabilities of appellant bank because respondent's Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation petition for the order presented a prima facie showing under the statute that appellant's capital was impaired. Appellant was not denied due process because it had notice of the hearing and chose not to appear or request a continuance.

 

1014 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Cumero v. Public Employment Relations Bd.


No. AO16723.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


204 Cal. App. 3d 87; 213 Cal. Rptr. 326; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1925



April 23, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted July 11, 1985 (See 49 Cal. 3d 575)


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion has been Reprinted for the Original Opinion of April 23, 1985, previously reported at 167 Cal. App. 3d 131 and Reprinted at 183 Cal. App. 3d 581 and Reprinted at 192 Cal. App. 3d 1542.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of an order of respondent Public Employment Relations Board in an action that challenged the withholding of a portion of his paycheck as a service fee pursuant to the Educational Employment Relations Act, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 2540-3549.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee was employed be a school district but was not a member of a union. The collective bargaining agreement between the union and the school district required a service fee equal to union dues to be withheld from a nonmember's paycheck. Petitioner filed an unfair practice charge with respondent Public Employment Relations Board alleging that a portion of the service fee was spent of activities not directly related to negotiation, contract administration and grievance handling. After the board ruled against the majority of petitioner's claims, he filed a petition for writ of review. The court vacated the order of respondent. The court held that the union had the burden to prove what proportion of the expenditures went to activities that could properly be charged to a nonmember. The court held that a public school employee union could spend the fees for lobbying and to pay dues to national affiliates. The court held that the fees could not be spent for union organizing and recruiting activities or to publish materials that did not relate to bargaining with the employer. The court also held that the automatic deduction of fees from petitioner's paycheck was proper.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order of respondent Public Employment Relations Board and remanded the matter for a new hearing. Respondent improperly placed the burden of proving which union expenditures were not a proper use of the service fee on petitioner employee; service fee could be used for lobbying expenses and national affiliate dues but could not be used for union organizing and recruiting activities.

 

1015 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Sherman


Crim. No. B004344


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


167 Cal. App. 3d 10; 212 Cal. Rptr. 861; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1914



April 17, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. M 253670, Michael Pirosh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of extended commitment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which extended by two years his commitment to the department of mental health. Appellant was convicted of child molestation, Cal. Penal Code § 288, found to be a mentally disordered sex offender pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6300, and committed for a maximum of five years.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which extended by two years appellant's commitment to the department of mental health. Appellant had been convicted of child molestation, Cal. Penal Code § 288, found to be a mentally disordered sex offender (MDSO) pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6300, and committed for a maximum of five years. Appellant contended, inter alia, that the extension of his commitment constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The court found that the MDSO extension commitment statutes did not impose cruel and unusual punishment upon appellant, reasoning that it was not unusual for mentally ill persons who were dangerous to be subject to potential confinement for indefinite periods of time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which extended by two years appellant's commitment to the department of mental health. The mentally disordered sex offender extension commitment statutes did not impose cruel and unusual punishment. It was not unusual for mentally ill persons who are dangerous to be subject to potential confinement for indefinite periods of time.

 

1016 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Inst. in Basic Youth Conflicts v. State Bd. of Equalization


No. B005675


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven


166 Cal. App. 3d 1093; 213 Cal. Rptr. 98; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1899



April 16, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied May 15, 1985, and the opinion was modified to read as printed below. The petition of plaintiff and appellant for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 25, 1985.
As corrected March 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 401896, Carlos E. Velarde, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of equalization sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ordered appellant to refund sales and use taxes, plus interest, of taxes paid by respondent nonprofit religious corporation under protest. Respondent challenged the trial court's decision denying its motion to amend its complaint after trial but prior to entry of judgment.


OVERVIEW: Respondent nonprofit religious corporation filed suit against appellant board of equalization which had imposed sales and use taxes on respondent's sale of its seminar syllabus and religious literature. After the trial court granted respondent a refund plus interest and denied respondent's motion to amend its complaint, both parties sought review. The court found that respondent was exempt from sales tax because the privilege of engaging in religious activity was guaranteed in the Constitution and respondent could not have been taxed for the privilege of doing that which it had the right to do. The court found that respondent was liable for use taxes because the tax was imposed on the storage, use, or other consumption of tangible personal property. The court reversed and remanded on the amount of the use refund to which respondent was entitled because there was substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that respondent was a consumer rather than a retailer for use tax purposes. The court ruled that respondent failed to show an abuse of discretion in the denial of respondent's motion to amend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that respondent nonprofit religious corporation was exempt from sales tax because it could not be taxed for engaging in First Amendment activities. The court reversed and remanded on respondent's use tax liability and amount of the use refund because the use tax was not a privilege tax and respondent was liable as a consumer. The court affirmed the denial of respondent's motion to amend as no abuse of discretion was shown.

 

1017 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Selleck v. Globe Int'l


No. B008350


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven


166 Cal. App. 3d 1123; 212 Cal. Rptr. 838; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1901



April 16, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 1, 1985. Kaus, J., Broussard, J., and Grodin, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C-441182, Leon Savitch and Ricardo A. Torres, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of dismissal of the second cause of action is affirmed. The judgment of dismissal of the first cause of action is reversed with directions to the trial court to overrule the demurrer as to that cause of action and allow defendant to answer. Plaintiff shall recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff celebrity's father sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed his causes of action against defendant publisher in an action for libel and invasion of privacy by depicting plaintiff in a false light.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff celebrity's father filed suit against defendant publisher for libel and false light invasion of privacy based on an article published in defendant's tabloid about the celebrity attributed to plaintiff. The superior court sustained defendant's demurrers and dismissed the action. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal of plaintiff's libel claim and affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's claims for false light invasion of privacy. The court held that, under the circumstances of its publication, defendant's article, including the headline and caption, were reasonably susceptible of a defamatory meaning and, thus, were libelous per se. Moreover, such article, headlines, and caption did not merely express defendant's opinion that plaintiff made statements about his son, but they falsely asserted as a fact that plaintiff made the statements. The dismissal of plaintiff's claim for false light invasion of privacy was proper, not because plaintiff failed to allege special damages as determined by the superior court, but because the claim was in effect a duplication of plaintiff's libel claim. Because the false light invasion of privacy claim was surplusage it was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the complaint by plaintiff celebrity's father for libel because defendant publisher's article, including the headline and caption, under the circumstances of its publication were reasonably susceptible of a defamatory meaning and were libelous per se. The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff's claim for false light invasion of privacy because such claim was a duplication of the libel claim.

 

1018 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Magnani v. Superior Court


Civ. No. B006741.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


166 Cal. App. 3d 905; 212 Cal. Rptr. 782; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1885



April 15, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rev. den. July 9, 1985 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insured sought a writ of mandate to direct respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to vacate its order that compelled arbitration in an action arising from a denial of coverage by real party in interest health insurer. Petitioner contended that he had a right to bring his action in a court of law and that the documents and representations of real party in interest's agents concerning his rights were ambiguous.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner insured brought an action against real party in interest health insurer to contest a denial of benefits. Real party in interest petitioned the trial court to compel arbitration of the dispute, and the petition was granted. Petitioner then sought a writ of mandate to direct the trial court to vacate the order compelling arbitration. The court granted the writ and directed the trial court to vacate the order. The court found that the information provided to petitioner in writing, in the form of a brochure and a certificate of insurance, and the oral representations of the agent differed as to the remedies available to petitioner to contest the denial of coverage. The court determined that the discrepancies created an ambiguity concerning procedures to contest denial of coverage that had to be resolved against real party in interest. The court concluded that the resolution of ambiguous information against real party in interest constituted a waiver of the right to arbitrate and that petitioner was entitled to have his action heard in a court of law. The court found that the trial court abused its discretion in compelling arbitration and directed it to vacate its order.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court abused its discretion in entering an order compelling arbitration in the action of petitioner insured against real party in interest health insurer, finding that an ambiguity existed between the documents provided to petitioner and representations by an agent concerning petitioner's recourse for denial of coverage, and that ambiguity had to be resolved against real party in interest.

 

1019 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Pittsburg Unified School Dist. v. California School Employees Assn.


Civ. No. 54671


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


166 Cal. App. 3d 875; 213 Cal. Rptr. 34; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1884



April 15, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied May 15, 1985, and respondents' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 18, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 221432, Robert Joseph Cooney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: As the record in this case demonstrates none of the grave abuses that provide occasion for permissible restriction of the liberties asserted by appellants under the First Amendment, and because appellants' activity did not seek to achieve an unlawful objective, 22 the judgment is reversed. The matter is remanded to the superior court, which is directed to dismiss the complaint for declaratory relief and damages.



22 Because of these conclusions it is unnecessary for us to address the question whether Code of Civil Procedure section 527.3 deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to issue the injunction it rendered. (Although this issue was raised below, appellants have not pursued it before us.) Nor, for the same reason, is it necessary for us to inquire whether the injunction, set forth, ante, at fn. 5, is unconstitutionally overbroad.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employees sought review after the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) issued a preliminary injunction prohibiting them, and others acting in concert with them, from picketing and leafleting outside the personal business offices of certain governing board members of respondent school district.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employees sought review after the trial court issued a preliminary injunction prohibiting them, and others acting in concert with them, from picketing and leafleting outside the personal business offices of certain governing board members of respondent school district. Appellants contended that the injunction violated their constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. I. The court found that there was no substantial evidence to show either that appellants intended an economic boycott of respondents' businesses, or that their activity actually adversely effected appellees' economic well being. Further, the court found that respondents failed to advance a tenable legal basis for their assertion that appellants' activity sought to achieve an unlawful purpose. Accordingly, the preliminary injunction was reversed and the matter was remanded with directions to dismiss respondents' complaint for declaratory relief and damages.


OUTCOME: The preliminary injunction against appellant employees was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to dismiss respondent school district's complaint because appellant's concerted activities did not constitute a corrupt practice or were otherwise unlawful. Accordingly, appellants' picketing and leafleting activities could not be restricted without infringing upon their First Amendment rights.

 

1020 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



In re Marriage of Mastropaolo


Civ. No. 33142


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


166 Cal. App. 3d 953; 213 Cal. Rptr. 26; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1889



April 15, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 11, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. FL 2854, Duke D. Rouse, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Insofar as the judgment awards wife a community property interest in the military retirement pension of husband it is affirmed. Upon condition that the foregoing judgment of affirmance becomes final, that part of the judgment awarding wife $ 700 per month spousal support is reversed for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. If for any cause the foregoing affirmance should not become final, that part of the trial court judgment awarding wife $ 700 per month spousal support is affirmed. If pursuant to this appellate judgment the portion of the judgment awarding wife $ 700 per month spousal support stands reversed and it appears husband has paid spousal support in excess of the amount eventually set, the trial court is directed to credit any such excess amount against the equalizing payment of $ 77,590.28 specified in the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband appeals from a judgment by the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which awarded respondent wife, 43.65 percent community property interest in the part of his military disability retirement pension that would have been paid to him as longevity retirement benefits had he so elected and a monthly payment spousal support.


OVERVIEW: In a divorce proceeding the trial court determined that a portion of the retirement benefits appellant husband could have received as longevity retirement pay was community property, awarding to respondent wife a 43.65 percent interest. The court affirmed holding that federal law did not prohibit the disposition ordered by the trial court in the circumstances of the case, where the military spouse retired before dissolution of the marriage and at the time he retired was eligible both for longevity and disability retirement and could have elected to receive longevity retirement benefits. The court held that in these circumstances the nonmilitary spouse had an interest in the retirement benefits recognized under both federal and state law which the military spouse could not destroy by his election to receive disability retirement benefits. Upon the condition that the foregoing judgment of affirmance became final, that part of the judgment awarding wife monthly spousal support was reversed for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement awarding wife a community property interest in the military retirement pension of husband holding that wife's rights were vested and the election of husband could not preempt her rights according to state law. The court reversed for further proceedings consistent with the opinion, the award of the monthly support on the condition that the foregoing judgment of affirmance became final.

 

1021 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Dubreuil v. West Winds Mobile Lodge


Civ. No. 31446.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


204 Cal. App. 3d 108; 213 Cal. Rptr. 12; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1879



April 11, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted Aug. 15, 1985 (L.A. 32095)
Trans. May 24, 1989 to Ct. App., 4th Dist., Div. 1, with directions to vacate its opn. and reconsider in light of Schmidt v. Superior Court (1989) 48 Cal. 3d 370.
Opinion filed February 5, 1990 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N 23857, Daniel J. Kremer, Judge.

This Opinion has been Reprinted for the Original Opinion of April 11, 1985, previously reported at 166 Cal. App. 3d 823 and Reprinted at 183 Cal. App. 3d 616 and Reprinted at 192 Cal. App. 3d 1576.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenants sought review of the order from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied them damages, an injunction, and declaratory relief against respondent landlord. Appellants contended that Cal. Civ. Code § 798.76, under which respondent had prevented appellants from selling their mobile home to a person who had children, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant tenants sought review of the order that denied them damages, an injunction, and declaratory relief against respondent landlord. Appellants sought to sell their mobile home to a person with children. Respondent restricted tenancy in the mobile home park to adults only, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 798.76. Appellants argued that § 798.76 was unconstitutional and was inconsistent with the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 51, prohibiting all arbitrary discrimination by businesses. The court affirmed the judgment and held that § 798.76 was a later enacted specific statute that prevailed over § 51, a general statute covering the same subject. The court held that § 798.76 allowed respondent to limit its mobile home park to adults only, in plain clear language not susceptible to misunderstanding. The court held that this restriction did not violate appellants' right to housing because there was no fundamental right to housing. The court held that § 798.76 was rationally related to the legitimate public purpose of assisting older citizens with their special housing needs and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the adults-only restriction on tenancy in respondent landlord's mobile home park was rationally related to a legitimate public purpose. Appellant tenants' constitutional rights were not violated because there was no fundamental right to housing.

 

1022 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Mun. Court


No. AO24300.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


166 Cal. App. 3d 610; 183 Cal. App. 3d 602; 192 Cal. App. 3d 1563; 212 Cal. Rptr. 631; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1862



April 8, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted June 28, 1985 (S.F. 24900)
Reprinted without change in 183 Cal. App. 3d 602, to permit tracking pending review by Supreme Ct.
Reprinted without change in 192 Cal. App. 3d 1563, to permit tracking pending review by Supreme Ct. (See 46 Cal. 3d 64)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner criminal defendant sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent Municipal Court for the San Francisco Judicial District of the City and County of San Francisco (California), to consider her for a diversion program under Cal. Penal Code § 1001 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner criminal defendant was charged with misdemeanor and felony offenses. The felonies were reduced to misdemeanors but, when petitioner applied for diversion under Cal. Penal Code § 1001 et seq., the application was denied under prosecution guidelines that prohibited diversion for persons originally charged with felonies. Petitioner sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent trial court to consider her for diversion. The court first found that the guideline conflicted with the express terms of Cal. Penal Code § 17(b)(5), which stated that a reduced misdemeanor was a misdemeanor for all purposes. The court also found that a prosecution-generated guideline, which absolutely precluded diversion for defendants originally charged with felonies that were reduced to misdemeanors, unlawfully impinged on the doctrine of separation of powers. Once a decision to charge was made, disposition of the case, whether through diversion or other means, was a judicial function, and the local prosecutor could not try to affect that authority by altering or mandating diversion eligibility. The writ of mandate was issued.


OUTCOME: The writ of mandate was issued. The court held that the guideline under which petitioner criminal defendant's request for diversion was denied was invalid as being in conflict with controlling statutes and, to the extent it allowed the prosecutor to alter or mandate diversion eligibility, unlawfully impinged on the doctrine of separation of powers in violation of the California Constitution.

 

1023 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Camenisch


Crim. No. F002682


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


166 Cal. App. 3d 594; 212 Cal. Rptr. 616; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1861



April 5, 1985 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Part I of this opinion is not published as it does not meet the standards for publication. (Cal. Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1.)


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied June 20, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 22760, Gerald K. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence from the Superior Court of Kern County (California) for murder with special circumstances, robbery, burglary, and sentence of life in prison without the possibility of parole. The court also imposed an additional one-year term for use of a knife and imposed, but stayed separate sentences on the robbery and burglary convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder with the special circumstances that defendant committed the murder during the commission of a robbery and a burglary. The information separately charged robbery and burglary; it also contained allegations that defendant personally used a knife in committing each offense. After the trial court denied defendant's motions to strike the special circumstances, to suppress confessions, to suppress evidence, and to grant defendant other forms of relief, defendant pleaded guilty to murder, robbery, and burglary. Defendant also admitted to the special circumstance and that he personally used a knife in the commission of the murder. Defendant was sentenced in accord with his plea bargain. On appeal, he urged that his conviction should be reversed and he be allowed to withdraw his guilty plea because he was not adequately advised of the effect of his guilty plea on his right to appeal and that he should be able to withdraw his admission to the special circumstance because he was incorrectly advised of the elements of the special circumstance. This court concluded that defendant's contentions were unmeritorious and affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of murder with special circumstances, robbery, and burglary was affirmed because defendant was adequately advised of the effect of his guilty plea on his right to appeal and he was correctly advised of the elements of the special circumstance.

 

1024 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Carroll v. State Bar


Civ. No. 31635


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


166 Cal. App. 3d 1193; 213 Cal. Rptr. 305; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1907



April 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied May 2, 1985. Lucas, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N22139, Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C455587, Fiorenzo V. Lopardo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; the superior court is directed to enter judgment for the State Bar of California. Pursuant to oral stipulation of the parties, the judgment is final immediately.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Bar of California challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), declaring that the Funds for the Provision of Legal Services to the Indigent Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6210 et seq., created a voluntary, not mandatory, program for depositing nominal, short-term client trust funds, like those of respondent clients, in an account. The interest was used to fund approved indigent legal services.


OVERVIEW: The Funds for the Provision of Legal Services to the Indigent Act (Act), Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6210 et seq., established an Interest on Lawyer Trust Account Program or IOLTA for pooling nominal, short-term client trust funds to generate interest income for funding indigent legal programs. Respondent clients sued appellant State Bar of California, which adopted professional conduct rules pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6211, pertaining to the use of IOLTA accounts. The trial court held that the Act established a voluntary, not mandatory, program for depositing nominal, short-term client funds, whose interest supported indigent legal services. Appellant challenged the decision. The court reversed and held that the Act unambiguously created a mandatory program. Section 6211 was not unconstitutionally vague. The Act did not involve a taking of property prohibited by U. S. Const. amend. V. Nor were respondents denied equal protection because no fundamental interest was impinged by mandating that nominal, short-term deposits be placed in an unsegregated interest-bearing account. The Act was not a restriction upon legal services or a denial of respondents' right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against appellant State Bar of California and held that the language of the Funds for the Provision of Legal Services to the Indigent Act (Act) was plain and unambiguous. The Act prescribed a mandatory pooling of minimal, short-term client trust funds to generate interest income for funding indigent legal services. The court rejected the constitutional issues raised by respondent clients.

 

1025 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Bestelmeyer


Crim. No. 44384


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


166 Cal. App. 3d 520; 212 Cal. Rptr. 605; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1854



April 3, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified April 25, 1985. Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied June 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. 17765, Charles R. McGrath, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Ventura County (California), which convicted him of 25 various sex offenses and sentenced him to 129 years in prison. Defendant claimed that the lengthy sentence constituted cruel and inhuman punishment and that his confession was involuntary and should not have been received into evidence.


OVERVIEW: Based on the evidence that defendant had sexually abused his stepdaughter repeatedly over a long period of time, defendant was convicted of 25 various sex offenses and sentenced to a total of 129 years in prison. Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence, asserting that his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment and that his confession was involuntary and should not have been received into evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. Defendant's reference to a lawyer during his interview with the investigation officers was patently ambiguous. There was substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that defendant did not intend to invoke his constitutional right to have an attorney present before he talked to the police officers, that he knowingly waived his right to counsel, and that he voluntarily confessed to the investigation officers. Consecutive prison terms totaling 129 years imposed as punishment for the commission of the 25 separate serious sex offenses was not cruel or unusual punishment and did not violate Cal. Const. art. I, § 17.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for 25 various sex offenses and his sentence of 129 years in prison. Defendant's confession was voluntary, and his reference to a lawyer during his interview with the investigation officers was not an indication that he wished to invoke his right to counsel because the reference was patently ambiguous. The lengthy sentence imposed upon defendant was not cruel or unusual under the circumstances.

 

1026 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Hyde


Crim. No. 15546


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


166 Cal. App. 3d 463; 212 Cal. Rptr. 440; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1848



April 1, 1985 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Certified for publication with the exception of section III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied July 10, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR 59071, Benjamin W. Hamrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that convicted him of first-degree murder, assault with force likely to produce great bodily injury, and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree murder, assault with force likely to produce great bodily harm, and false imprisonment. Defendant did not testify at trial. The testimony of the witnesses he called on his behalf was marginally relevant and did nothing to detract from the essence of the prosecution's case. The jury returned verdicts of guilty on all counts. On appeal, defendant made three contentions regarding the correctness of the instructions given to the jury on which it was to base its verdict on the first-degree murder charge. He argued that certain instructions, alternative theories of first-degree murder, should not have been given and that certain instructions, voluntary manslaughter, should have been. He also contended that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on premeditated first-degree murder. The court concluded that the trial court did not err. Defendant also challenged the court's decision to inform prospective jurors prior to voir dire that the death penalty was not involved in the murder case. The court concluded that the court's comments were proper and prudent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first-degree murder even though the body of the victim was never found because the jury instructions were proper and the trial court's decision to inform prospective jurors prior to voir dire that the death penalty was not involved in the murder case was proper and prudent.

 

1027 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Grupe v. Cal. Coastal Com


No. A019818


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


166 Cal. App. 3d 148; 212 Cal. Rptr. 578; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1821



March 27, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied April 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Cruz County, No. 73098, Donald O. May and Roland K. Hall, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgments in favor of respondent on the first and second causes of action and the order awarding attorney's fees are reversed, and the trial court is ordered to enter judgment in favor of appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state coastal commission challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Cruz County, No. 73098 (California), which found that its permit issued to respondent land owner, requiring that respondent set aside a portion of his land for public use was an unconstitutional taking, and in violation of state administrative law.


OVERVIEW: Respondent landowner applied for a permit to build a single house residence on his beachfront property. Appellant state coastal commission granted the permit, with the condition that respondent set aside a portion of his land for public use. Respondent objected to the condition of the permit, and filed suit. The trial court found that the condition was an unconstitutional taking, and made in violation of state administrative law. Appellant challenged the ruling, and the court held that so long as a project contributed to the need for public access, even if the project standing alone had not created the need for access, and even if there was only an indirect relationship between the access exacted and the need to which the project contributed, imposition of an appellant's access condition on respondent's development permit was sufficiently related to burdens created by the project to be constitutional. The court stated that there was no unconstitutional taking, requiring that the public to bare the burden for the costs. The court also concluded that the permit was enacted in compliance with state administrative law and that it was valid. The court denied respondent attorneys fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellant's state coastal commission's conditional building permit issued to respondent to set aside a portion of his land for public use was not an unconstitutional taking, did not violate substantive due process, and was not enacted in violation of state administrative law. The court upheld the restriction, and denied respondent attorneys fees.

 

1028 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Morris v. Castro


Nos. A025695, A027818


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Five


166 Cal. App. 3d 33; 212 Cal. Rptr. 299; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1811



March 26, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 28, 1985. Respondent's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied June 20, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County, Nos. 110443, 115988, Henry J. Broderick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order granting summary judgment in Morris et al. v. Castro (A025695) is reversed. The order granting the petition for writ of habeas corpus in In re Ellis (A027818) is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Marin County (California) that granted respondents, life prisoners, summary judgment and/or a writ of habeas corpus determining that Cal. Penal Code § 3041.5 violated federal and state proscriptions against ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: Respondents were prisoners who received life sentences, mostly for murder and other serious crimes. The legislature amended Cal. Penal Code § 3041.5, changing the requirement for annual parole suitability hearings to permit the Board of Prison Terms (board) to schedule hearings every two or three years where the board determined that it was not reasonable to expect that parole would be granted the following years. Respondents contended that the amended law violated federal and state proscriptions against ex post facto laws. The trial court granted respondents summary judgment. The court reversed holding that the amended law effected a procedural change only and no substantive right was affected. The board always had the discretion to retain a prisoner for the maximum period and respondents could not claim they had a reasonable expectation of an earlier parole release.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment grant to respondents. The court held that respondents could not claim they had a reasonable expectation of an earlier parole release. The amended law effected a procedural change only and no substantive right was affected.

 

1029 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Harris


No. A022241


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Five


165 Cal. App. 3d 1246; 212 Cal. Rptr. 216; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1806



March 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' petitions for review by the Supreme Court were denied May 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 110375, Jack K. Berman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order setting aside the information is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people sought review of an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) setting aside the information against appellee on the ground that Cal. Penal Code § 872(b) was unconstitutional. Appellees asserted that the statute violated their constitutional right of confrontation, right of due process, and privilege against self-incrimination.


OVERVIEW: Appellees allegedly broke into a car with the intent to commit larceny. At their preliminary hearing, the prosecutor requested that the magistrate admit in evidence a written statement of the owner of the car under the provisions of Cal. Penal Code § 872. The magistrate admitted the statement, rejecting appellees' motion to exclude. Appellees were jointly charged with violating Cal. Penal Code § 459. Appellees then filed a motion to set aside the information against them. The magistrate granted the motion on the ground that Cal. Penal Code § 872(b) was unconstitutional. The court reversed the order setting aside the information. The statute, which specified the circumstances in which a written statement could be used at a preliminary examination and set forth the rights and duties of the defense if the prosecution attempted to use such a written statement, was constitutional. It did not violate appellees' state or federal right of confrontation, right of due process, or privilege against self-incrimination, but rather was an attempt to rejuvenate the long-resolved contemporaneous cross-examination controversy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order setting aside the information against appellee, finding that the superior court erred in holding the statute governing the admission of witness statements at preliminary examinations unconstitutional. The statute did not violate appellees' federal or state right of confrontation, right of due process, or privilege against self-incrimination.

 

1030 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Amusing Sandwich v. City of Palm Springs


No. E000676


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


165 Cal. App. 3d 1116; 211 Cal. Rptr. 911; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1796



March 22, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Riverside County, No. I-36419, John P. Carroll, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arcade appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) in plaintiff's injunctive action to prevent enforcement of defendant city's ordinance, which held that plaintiff violated defendant's ordinance against the installation of more than four video games in one commercial business in the business district and enjoined plaintiff from maintaining more than four on its premises on defendant's cross-complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff arcade brought an action against defendant city, seeking an injunction to prevent the enforcement of an ordinance which limited installation of video games in the business district to four games or less. Defendant filed a cross-complaint, claiming that plaintiff's violation of the ordinance was a nuisance per se. The trial court found for defendant and permanently enjoined plaintiff from maintaining more than four video games on its premises. Plaintiff appealed from the decision. The court affirmed, holding that equal protection and due process rights were not violated because the ordinance was not arbitrary or unreasonable. The planning commission's resolution defining secondary use of video games as four games or less was not an unconstitutional delegation of authority by defendant, because there was no evidence that the decision to issue the certificate of occupancy by defendant was based on the planning commission's resolution. The ordinance was not void for vagueness because it was detailed. By failing to controvert defendant's allegation that plaintiff's use of 25 video games was a violation of the zoning ordinance, plaintiff admitted the violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that plaintiff arcade's constitutional rights to due process and equal protection were not violated by defendant city's ordinance limiting the number of video games in a commercial business to four. The court found that the ordinance was not vague and plaintiff admitted to violating the ordinance.

 

1031 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Am. Nat'l Bank v. Peacock


Civ. No. F003696


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


165 Cal. App. 3d 1206; 212 Cal. Rptr. 97; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1803



March 22, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Kern County, No. 144231, Marvin E. Ferguson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded for recalculation of interest on the judgment pursuant to the opinion expressed herein. Appellant to recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of an order by the Superior Court of Kern County (California) which increased the interest set pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §685.010 on a judgment entered in favor of respondent.


OVERVIEW: In September 1979, a judgment was entered against appellant bank and interest on the judgment was set a 7 percent per annum from March 14, 1977, to the date of judgment. In September 1983, the interest was set to increase to 10 percent after September 1979. Appellant was partly successful in reducing the interest from the 10 percent demanded; however, this order was amended and the interest rate was increased to 10 percent after December 31, 1981. Appellant contended that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §685.010, which changed the interest rate from 7 to 10 percent, became effective on January 1, 1983. If so, the court should not have increased the rate to 10 percent on January 1, 1982. The court reversed and remanded the judgment for recalculation of interest on the judgment pursuant to the January 1, 1983, enactment date because the legislative history excluded the possibility that retroactive effect was intended. The preenactment opinion, an amended version of §685.0101, a memorandum by the Attorney General's Officer, and an opinion by the legislative counsel all demonstrated that January 1, 1983, was the correct date and any mention to January 1, 1982, was an oversight.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment increasing the interest on the judgment entered against appellant was reversed and remanded for recalculation because retroactive effect of a statute regarding an increase in judgment interest was not intended to be retroactive to January 1, 1982.

 

1032 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



In re Demond


No. B007959


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


165 Cal. App. 3d 932; 211 Cal. Rptr. 680; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1782



March 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied April 4, 1985, and respondent's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied May 23, 1985. Reynoso, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.



DISPOSITION:  The order to show cause, having served its purpose, is discharged; the petition for a writ of habeas corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought a writ of habeas corpus from the court after petitioner claimed he was entitled to be represented by counsel at a hearing conducted to determine his parole release date under the indeterminate sentencing law that was in effect at the time that petitioner was convicted to life imprisonment for first degree murder.
