People v. Guilford


Crim. No. 40260


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


151 Cal. App. 3d 406; 198 Cal. Rptr. 700; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1560



January 30, 1984 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion has been certified for publication with the exception of issues I, II, and III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied March 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A-559419, Richard Montes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appellant's sentence is modified to the extent that the enhancement for use of a deadly weapon (§ 12022, subd. (b)) imposed as to count I is ordered stayed. The judgment as modified is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that upheld a jury verdict that found appellant guilty of attempted robbery and first-degree murder and imposed an enhanced sentence based on use of a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and a cohort attempted to rob a man and a woman who were waiting for a bus. Cohort accosted the man with a knife. Appellant held the woman with one hand and was pulling at her purse with the other. A police car approached the group, and cohort was arrested. The woman was hit in the head with a tire iron by appellant who fled the scene. Two days later, the woman died from heart attack caused by stress and traumatic head injuries. Appellant was convicted of attempted robbery and first-degree murder by a jury. The trial court imposed an enhanced sentence based on use of a deadly weapon. The court affirmed the convictions, but modified by staying the deadly weapon enhancement holding that failure to stay an enhancement where the base term was stayed, had the effect of elevating the enhancement to the status of an offense. Enhancements were not offenses, but were punishments.


OUTCOME: The court stayed the deadly weapon enhancement, but otherwise affirmed appellant's convictions, holding that enhancements were not offenses, but were punishments. The failure to stay an enhancement, where the base term is stayed, had the effect of elevating the enhancement to the status of an offense.

 

1188 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Lander v. Dep't of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 28458.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


151 Cal. App. 3d 325; 198 Cal. Rptr. 810; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1550



January 26, 1984 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted. Mar. 22, 1984 (L.A. 31884)
Opn. filed Sept. 24, 1985, not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Imperial County, No. 2886, William E. Lehnhardt, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Imperial County (California), which upheld respondent Department of Motor Vehicles' suspension of her driving privilege for one year under Cal. Veh. Code § 13352(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant licensee argued that her driver's license was wrongfully suspended because Cal. Veh. Code § 13352(a)(3) was only applicable to violations of Cal. Veh. Code § 23152 punishable under Cal. Veh. Code § 23165; the 1982 amendments could not be retroactively applied to suspend her license; and respondent Department of Motor Vehicles' (DMV) reliance on the 1982 amendments to the Vehicle Code constituted the application of an ex post facto law. The court found that only the statutory numbering of the violation was changed by the 1982 amendment, so a conviction under former Cal. Veh. Code § 23102 constituted a conviction under § 23152. The court found that the DMV's application of the 1982 amendment to appellant's second drunk driving offense occurring before the amendment date directly contravened the rule against retroactive application of a statute, absent a clear legislative intent. The court reversed and concluded there was no statutory authority for the DMV to impose a penalty predicated on an act committed before the effective date of the 1982 version of § 13352(a)(3).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court. The court concluded that respondent, Department of Motor Vehicles, could not apply a statute retroactively to suspend the driver's license of appellant licensee.

 

1189 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Tirado


Crim. Nos. 15210, 15556


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


151 Cal. App. 3d 341; 198 Cal. Rptr. 682; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1552



January 26, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petitions for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied March 22, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 58798, Susan P. Finlay, Judge. ++


++ Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed and petition for writ of habeas corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of robbery by the Superior Court of San Diego County, (California). Defendant contended his plea of guilty to robbery was void and violated due process because it was the result of presumptive, as well as actual, vindictive prosecution. Defendant also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, on grounds, of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to robbery of a store and appealed. At the time of his conviction he was serving time for robbery of a gas station, for which he had requested and received the intermediate five-year term, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1170 (b) and Cal. Penal Code § 1204. On appeal defendant contended that the shoe store robbery charge was filed solely in retaliation for defendant's exercise of his legal right to request the intermediate sentence for the gas station robbery. The court affirmed the conviction and denied defendant's petition for habeas corpus. The court held that no connection was found between the two sets of crimes with which defendant was charged, and they were not part of the same act or a course of conduct. The prosecution could have sought defendant's indictment for either robbery at any time before the statute of limitations had run, subject only to the due process constraint requiring the statute of limitations not be invoked to curtail the self-executing constitutional guaranty of the right to a speedy trial. The court also held that defendant was not harmed by his trial counsel's failure to raise the vindictive prosecution defense below.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of robbery was affirmed, and his petition for habeas corpus was denied. The court found that vindictive prosecution rules were not applicable to the facts of this case, because the second indictment arose out of separate, distinct, criminal acts. The court also held that the claim of ineffective assistance of counsel failed because defendant was not harmed by counsel's failure to raise a vindictive prosecution defense.

 

1190 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



In re Krall


Civ. No. 67604


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


151 Cal. App. 3d 792; 199 Cal. Rptr. 91; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1598



January 24, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County, No. 19169, Warren C. Conklin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mentally retarded person challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California), which involuntarily committed defendant to a state hospital pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6500. Defendant asserted that the trial court incorrectly instructed the jury regarding the definition of mental retardation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant objected to the definition of "mental retardation" given by the trial court in the action that involuntarily committed defendant because he adjudicated mentally retarded and dangerous pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6500. The court found that mental retardation had long had a generally accepted technical meaning referring to significantly subaverage general intellectual functioning existing concurrently with deficits in adaptive behavior and appearing in the developmental period. It further found that the inquiry into the degree of mental retardation and dangerousness mandated by § 6507 strongly suggested that periodically, treating physicians and other witnesses must be produced in court in order to testify as to the present mental condition and potential danger from the subject. Therefore, the court held that because no qualified expert testified, there was no evidentiary foundation for the jury's finding of mental retardation. Because the incorrect definition was given to the jury, the court reversed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that involuntarily committed defendant to a state mental hospital. The court held that expert testimony was necessary to provide an evidentiary foundation for finding mental retardation and that the trial court provided the wrong definition of mentally retarded.

 

1191 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Itt World Communications v. City & County of San Francisco


No. AO17703.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


151 Cal. App. 3d 1; 198 Cal. Rptr. 426; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1526



January 23, 1984 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Apr. 19, 1984 (See 37 Cal. 3d 859)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 771841, Ira A. Brown, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility taxpayer brought suit in the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) for a refund of property taxes paid to the respondent county and city, based on an assessment made by respondent State Board of Equalization, on the basis that Cal. Const. art. XIII A required a rollback to 1975 property values. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of respondents, and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer, a public utility which paid property taxes to respondent county based on an assessment by respondent State Board of Equalization (Board) filed a petition with the Board contending that Cal. Const. art. XIII A required a rollback of the assessed value of appellant's property to 1975-1976 values. The Board denied appellant's petitions, and appellant filed suit in the trial court. The trial court granted summary judgment for respondents, and appellant sought review. The court reversed the judgment, holding that although appellant was assessed by the state, the rollback of taxes to 1975-1976 values applied to appellant. Considering article XIII A as a whole, the court held that the phrase "county assessor's valuation" was intended only to designate a specific numerical figure to which property owners could look to determine their new tax basis. The court concluded that Cal. Const. art. XIII A, § 2(a) could reasonably be construed to apply to state-assessed real property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of respondents and remanded the case to the superior court with directions to remand to the State Board of Equalization. The court held that Proposition 13 applied to state-assessed public utilities as well as county-assessed properties, and that appellant's assessment should be rolled back to 1975-1976 values.

 

1192 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harrison


Crim. No. 12656.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD Dist.


150 Cal. App. 3d 1142; 198 Cal. Rptr. 762; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1523



January 20, 1984 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As modified Jan. 24, 1984; Hg. granted Apr. 19, 1984 (Crim. 23652)
Opn. filed March 14, 1986 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 64326, Rothwell B. Mason, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) for attempted robbery with a deadly weapon. The trial court found true the allegation that defendant had previously been convicted of a serious felony under Cal. Penal Code § 667, and sentenced defendant to eight years in prison. Defendant appealed, challenging the admission of his prior conviction under the newly-enacted Cal. Const. art. I, § 28(f).


OVERVIEW: Defendant held a man at knife-point and tried to empty his pockets. Defendant was convicted of attempted robbery with a deadly weapon. Cal. Penal Code §§ 211, 213, and 12022(b). Defendant had previously been convicted of a serious felony under Cal. Penal Code § 667, and was sentenced to eight years in prison. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. The imposition of a five-year enhancement for defendant's prior conviction was proper, even though the enhancement had not been enacted when defendant pleaded guilty in the earlier case. Defendant's prior conviction was properly admitted for impeachment and enhancement purposes under Cal. Const. art. I, § 28(f), which effectively abrogated People v. Beagle, 492 P.2d 1 (1972) and its progeny. The court held that any felony, not just a felony implicating truthfulness, is admissible under § 28(f). The court held that "conviction" in § 28(f) meant a constitutionally valid conviction. Defendant's prior conviction should not have been sanitized; the court held that People v. Barrick, 654 P.2d 1243 (1982) had no continuing validity after the effective date of § 28(f).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction. Admission of defendant's prior conviction was proper under the clear mandate of Proposition 8; that proposition abrogated earlier cases circumscribing the circumstances under which prior felony convictions were admissible. The court held that convictions should no longer be sanitized; however, the error in sanitizing defendant's prior conviction actually benefitted defendant and did not require reversal.

 

1193 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Nissan Motor Corp. v. New Motor Vehicle Bd.


Civ. No. 53381


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


153 Cal. App. 3d 109; 202 Cal. Rptr. 1; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1759



January 19, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied February 16 and March 16, 1984, and petitions of real party in interest and appellant and interveners and appellants for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied April 18, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 770613, Jay A. Pfotenhauer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed insofar as it holds that the proceedings before the Board were unconstitutional (paragraphs (1) and (2). The provisions of the judgment commanding the Board to enter a new decision to the effect that good cause was shown for the termination of the franchise and Nissan Motor Corporation was entitled to terminate the franchise in dispute are reversed. The case is remanded for further proceedings before a Board acting without the participation of the new motor vehicle dealer members (§ 3010).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, dealer and New Motor Vehicle Board, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which was in favor of respondent manufacturer in an action concerning the termination of an automobile franchise.


OVERVIEW: Respondent manufacturer terminated the franchise of appellant dealer and filed a petition for writ of mandamus after appellant New Motor Vehicle Board found that respondent had not established that the requirements of the franchise were reasonable. The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it held that the proceedings before appellant board were unconstitutional, reversed the judgment commanding appellant board to enter a new decision, and remanded for further proceedings before respondent board acting without the participation of the car dealer members. The court concluded that appellant board was unlawfully constituted and that its procedure violated the basic precepts of due process to decide disputes between manufacturers and dealers. There was no provision that the manufacturers be represented on appellant board and the car dealer members could participate in, hear, and comment or advise other members upon any matter. The court found that the disparity in representation of the parties on appellant board created a substantial likelihood and/or appearance of bias rendering respondent board and its decision unconstitutional as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it held that the proceedings before appellant New Motor Vehicle Board were unconstitutional. The court, however, reversed the provisions of the judgment commanding appellant board to enter a new decision approving respondent manufacturer's termination of appellant dealer's franchise. The case was remanded for further proceedings before appellant board.

 

1194 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Atchley v. City of Fresno


Civ. No. 7374


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


151 Cal. App. 3d 635; 199 Cal. Rptr. 72; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1584



January 17, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 255611-6, Stephen Henry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant disability pension recipients sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which entered judgment in favor of respondent city in appellants' suit for declaratory, injunctive and compensatory relief under Fresno, Cal. Municipal Code § 2-1731(c).


OVERVIEW: In appellant disability pension recipients' suit for declaratory, injunctive, and compensatory relief under Fresno Municipal Code § 2-1731(c), the trial court entered judgment in favor of respondent city. The trial court held that requiring appellants to file reports of outside income, reducing pension payments based on said report, and withholding pension payments until the report was received, was lawful. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that respondent's practice was not a modification of appellants' contractual right to receive pension payments, but a preexisting term and condition of receiving disability benefits. The court held that withholding payments until receipt of the report did not constitute a seizure, only an enforcement of an existing policy. The court held that reducing payments based on outside income was not unconstitutionally discriminatory under Cal. Const. art. IV, § 16 or Cal. Const. art. I, § 7, appellants and active employees were not similarly situated. The court held that withholding pension payments did not violate Cal. Lab. Code § 216 because the facts did not indicate a wilful failure to pay wages due and payable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment in favor of respondent city in appellant disability pension recipients' suit for declaratory, injunctive and compensatory relief. Respondent's practice of requiring appellants to file reports of outside income, reducing benefits based on said report, and withholding benefits upon receipt of the report was a preexisting term and condition of receiving disability benefits, not a modification thereof.

 

1195 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shelton


Crim. No. 15322.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


150 Cal. App. 3d 946; 198 Cal. Rptr. 589; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 1506



January 13, 1984 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. den. Mar. 22, 1984; and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CRN 7736, Fiorenzo V. Lopardo, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted him of violating Cal. Veh. Code § 23153(a) by causing injury to another while driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of driving under the influence and causing injury to another in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23153. On appeal, he argued that the jury instruction was improper because it shifted the burden to him to prove he was not driving under the influence. The trial court instructed the jury that it should find defendant guilty if there was 0.10 percent or more alcohol in defendant's blood, unless it had reasonable doubt that defendant was under the influence. The court found that the statute establishing the presumption that a driver was under the influence of alcohol based on a chemical analysis of that person's blood or breath was constitutional because there was a rational connection between the fact proved and the ultimate fact presumed. The court also ruled the use of the word "shall" as it affected the burden of proof was a permissive presumption. The instruction made it clear that the prosecution had the burden of proof beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was under the influence and did not impermissibly shift the burden to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which convicted defendant of injuring another while driving under the influence of alcohol because statute, which created a presumption that a driver with a blood level of 0.10 percent alcohol was under the influence of alcohol, was a permissive inference.

Hale v. City of Santa Paula


Civ. No. 66687.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


159 Cal. App. 3d 1233; 206 Cal. Rptr. 265; 1984 Cal. App. LEXIS 2510

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Nov. 21, 1984 (L.A. 32003).

1197 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Ferrini v. City of San Luis Obispo


Civ. No. 68053


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


150 Cal. App. 3d 239; 197 Cal. Rptr. 694; 1983 Cal. App. LEXIS 2550



December 28, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County, No. 52034, Nathaniel O. Bradley, Judge. *


* Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of San Luis Obispo and appellant center sought review from the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California), which declared that a charter providing for voter approval of appellant City of San Luis Obispo's annexation of respondents' land was unconstitutional and held that the annexation was valid and effective.


OVERVIEW: Respondent landowners filed a petition for the annexation of their uninhabited land to appellant City of San Luis Obispo (City). Respondents' petition complied with the provisions of the Municipal Organization Act of 1977 (MORGA), Cal. Gov't Code §§ 35000 to 35500. The electorate of appellant City approved a charter, which provided for an election, at which the electorate rejected the annexation. The court affirmed the decision that the charter providing for an election on the proposed annexation was unconstitutional. MORGA embodied the exclusive procedure for annexation of territory to a city and precluded an election by the city voters in uninhabited annexations. MORGA provided for elections only in exceptional circumstances when inhabited territory was annexed and made no provision for an election when uninhabited territory was annexed. It was clearly the legislature's intent to occupy the field of annexation of territory by enacting MORGA, which meant appellant City's charter could not contain provisions pertaining to annexation which were contrary to the general laws of statewide application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the charter providing for voter approval of annexation was unconstitutional. The Municipal Organization Act of 1977 (MORGA) was the exclusive procedure for annexation of territory to a city and precluded an election by a municipality's voters concerning uninhabited annexations. The legislature clearly intended to occupy the field of territorial annexation.

 

1198 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Tinsley v. Superior Court


Civ. Nos. 50497, 50997


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


150 Cal. App. 3d 90; 197 Cal. Rptr. 643; 1983 Cal. App. LEXIS 2537



December 23, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied January 20, 1984, and the judgment was modified to read as printed above. The petitions of all appellants and of respondents Palo Alto Unified School District and Ravenswood City School District for a hearing by the Supreme Court were denied April 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 206010, Melvin E. Cohn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment sustaining respondent's demurrers and dismissing appellants' petition is reversed. The order denying appellants' motion for partial summary judgment is affirmed. The case is remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with the views expressed herein. Costs on appeal in both actions are awarded to appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents, sought review of order of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which dismissed their interdistrict segregation lawsuit on the ground that pursuant to Cal. Const. art. I, § 7, as amended by Proposal 1, appellants were required to show de jure segregation before the trial court could order desegregation remedies of busing or pupil reassignment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant parents sought review of a judgment dismissing their interdistrict segregation lawsuit. Appellants claimed that Cal. Const. art. I, § 7, as amended by Proposal 1, was unconstitutional. The court held that prior to Proposal 1, California had race related legislation that was not required by the Federal Constitution, and its repeal, requiring that appellants prove de jure segregation before courts could order mandatory school assignments and transportation, was not unconstitutional. The court also found that Proposal 1 did not violate the requirements for ballot initiatives in Cal. Elec. Code §§ 3570, 3572, which required that a voter's pamphlet include a "copy" and ballot summary for each initiative, and Cal. Const. art. II, § 10, which required the attorney general to prepare a summary of the chief purpose of the proposal. The court affirmed the order denying appellants' motion for partial summary judgment but held that because remedies other than mandatory school assignment and transportation were still available to cure alleged de facto segregation, it was error for the trial court to dismiss appellants' suit without leave to amend.


OUTCOME: The judgment sustaining respondent school district's demurrers and dismissing appellants, parents', petition was reversed because remedies other than pupil assignment and transportation were still available to cure alleged de facto segregation. The order denying appellants' motion for partial summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1199 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Perkey v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 22632.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD Dist.


150 Cal. App. 3d 74; 197 Cal. Rptr. 516; 1983 Cal. App. LEXIS 2535



December 22, 1983 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Mar. 15, 1984 (See 42 Cal. 3d 185)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 307275, Ronald W. Tochterman, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual filed a petition in the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) to compel defendant Department of Motor Vehicles to renew plaintiff's driver's license without requiring her to submit a thumb or fingerprint as mandated by Cal. Veh. Code § 12800(c). The superior court denied plaintiff's petition and plaintiff sought review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individual challenged the decision of the superior court, which refused to grant her petition to compel defendant Department of Motor Vehicles to renew her driver's license without regard to the requirements of Cal. Veh. Code § 12800(c). Specifically, § 12800(c) required that every application for a driver's license contain a legible print thumb or fingerprint. The trial court denied the petition and the appellate court affirmed, holding that § 12800 was facially constitutional. Applying a rational relationship test, the appellate court determined that § 12800(c) was reasonably related to the legitimate government purposes of deterring fraudulent applications for licenses, distinguishing between two or more licensed drivers having the same name and date of birth, and discovering when the same individual has been issued two driver's licenses. Also, § 12800(c) did not violate plaintiff's constitutional right to privacy under Cal. Const. art. I, § 1. Plaintiff had no constitutionally protected privacy interest in the information intrinsically contained in her fingerprint.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment, which denied plaintiff individual's petition seeking to compel the Department of Motor Vehicles to renew her driver's license without regard to the statutory requirement of a fingerprint. The statute was facially constitutional in that it was rationally related to the legitimate state purpose of identification and plaintiff had no constitutionally protected right to privacy in her fingerprint.

 

1200 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Travelers Ins. Co. v. Sierra Pac. Airlines


Civ. No. 67169


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


149 Cal. App. 3d 1144; 197 Cal. Rptr. 416; 1983 Cal. App. LEXIS 2516; 49 Cal. Comp. Cases 808



December 20, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C116674, Arthur K. Marshall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airline challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which was entered in favor of respondent insurance company and which allowed respondent to recover from appellant the amount it had been required to pay to the Department of Industrial Relations of the State of California pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 4706.5.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed in a crash involving one of appellant airline's planes. As the decedent had no dependents at the time of her death, respondent insurance company, which had issued a workers' compensation insurance policy to the decedent's employer, was required, pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 4706.5, to pay to the Department of Industrial Relations of the State of California a sum equal to the total dependency death benefit that would have been payable to the decedent's surviving dependent, had such a dependent existed. Thereafter, respondent filed suit against appellant to recover the monies it had paid out. The trial court ruled in respondent's favor. Appellant challenged that judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. Pursuant to Cal. Lab. Code § 3852, as amended, respondent could recover from appellant the money it had paid pursuant to § 4706.5. Under the facts, § 3852 provided an action for indemnity. Although § 4706.5 required respondent to make the payment to the state, rather than the decedent, the payment constituted compensation within the meaning of § 3852, as amended. Section 4706.5 did not impose upon appellant double liability and did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of respondent insurance company in its suit against appellant airline to recover the amount it had been required by statute to pay to the Department of Industrial Relations because the decedent, who had died in a plane crash, had no dependents at the time of her death. The applicable statute allowed respondent to recover the amount paid, and the statute did not violate equal protection.
